The Life and Journey of Imam al-Shafi'i
Biographical sketch of al-Shafi'i's travels and scholarly development

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace al-Shafi'i's major travels and identify the key scholars and schools he engaged with.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i's travels exposed him to diverse schools, shaping his unique synthesis of hadith and ra'y.

This passage traces al-Shafi'i's physical and intellectual journey from Iraq to Mecca to Egypt, highlighting how his encounters with scholars from different traditions formed the basis of his later mastery. Understanding his biography helps us see jadal not as mere rhetoric but as a skill rooted in comprehensive knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Locate the chronological sequence
Identify the key events: return from Iraq to Mecca, teaching in the Haram, meeting Ahmad ibn Hanbal, second trip to Baghdad, move to Egypt.
2
Identify the scholarly contexts of each location
Note which schools were dominant in each location: in Baghdad the Mu'tazila and Persian influence were strong, in Mecca he met scholars from various schools during Hajj, in Egypt he spread his knowledge.
3
Extract the praise from Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Dawud al-Zahiri
What virtues do they highlight? Ahmad calls him the reviver of the century and a philosopher; Dawud lists his unique combination of knowledge and character.
4
Connect his travels to his jadal skill
Explain how exposure to different methodologies (hadith school, ra'y school) enabled him to debate both sides effectively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عاد الشافعي من العراق إلى مكة، فأخذ يلقي دروسه في الحرم المكي ويلتقي بكبار العلماء في موسم الحج، وكان ممن التقى بهم أحمد بن حنبل، وقد ظل في إلقاء دروسه بمكة مدة طويلة ذكر الرواة أنها بلغت تسع سنين ظهرت فيها شخصيته في نضجه الفكري ومنهجه العلمي والفقهي ثم سافر إلى بغداد للمرة الثانية سنة 195هـ ، ولكن لم يطب له المقام فيها لغلبة العنصر الفارسي في عهد المأمون وما كان من تقريبه المعتزلة وميله إلى مناهج بحثهم، وقد دعي إلى مصر، فاستجاب للدعوة ورحل إليها، فنشر بها علمه رجب سنة 204 هـ ، وقد بلغ من العمر أربعًا وخمسين سنة كان في آخر عمره رحمه الله علما بين العلماء، لا يجارى في علمه؛ يقول فيه الإمام أحمد ابن حنبل: يروى عن النبي أن الله عز وجل يبعث لهذه الأمة على رأس كل مائة سنة رجلا يقيم لها أمر دينها، فكان عمر بن عبد العزيز على رأس المائة، وأرجو أن يكون الشافعي على رأس المائة الأخرى. ويقول أيضًا: الشافعي فيلسوف في أربعة أشياء في اللغة واختلاف الناس والمعاني والفقه، ويقول داود بن علي الظاهري: للشافعي من الفضائل ما لم يجتمع لغيره من شرف نسبه وصحة دينه ومعتقده وسخاوة نفسه ومعرفته بصحة الحديث وسقيمه وناسخه ومنسوخه، وحفظ الكتاب والسنة وسيرة الخلفاء، وحسن التصنيف. وخلال رحلة حياته؛ تقلب الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه بين بلدان مختلفة وأحوال كثيرة، وأخذ العلم والفقه ومباحث الشريعة من مدارس متنوعة وعن شيوخ كثيرين متعددي المناهج، وقد عايش ما قام في ذلك العهد من صراع ونزاع بين مدرسة الحديث ومدرسة الرأي، وتمرس بالجدل والمناظرة حتى أصبح مناظرًا من الطراز الأول، فشارك في المناظرات التي قامت بين علماء المدرستين فكان يجادل أهل العراق لإلمامه بالقرآن الكريم والسنة وبلاغتها، ويناظر أهل الحجاز لإدراكه الحكم الشرعية والعلل القياسية ولم يناظر أحدا إلا ظهر عليه، وكان يستفيد من موسم الحج أثناء إقامته في مكة وقدومه إليها ليجتمع مع كبار العلماء في العقيدة والحديث والفقه واللغة فيأخذ منهم ويأخذون منه، ويجادلهم ويناظرهم، فاجتمع فيه رجاحة العقل وسعة الاطلاع، وفصاحة اللسان، وقوة البيان، ورصانة الأسلوب وقد برع الشافعي في الجدل والمناظرة حتى فاق فيها أقرانه من العلماء في عصره، فقد ناظر أستاذه محمد بن الحسن في كثير من المسائل كما كانت له
Al-Shafi'i returned from Iraq to Mecca, and began to give his lessons in the Sacred Mosque, meeting with senior scholars during the Hajj season. Among those he met was Ahmad ibn Hanbal. He continued giving lessons in Mecca for a long period, which narrators said reached nine years, during which his personality appeared in his intellectual maturity and his scientific and juristic methodology. Then he traveled to Baghdad for the second time in the year 195 AH, but he did not find it pleasant to stay there because of the dominance of the Persian element in the era of al-Ma'mun and his drawing close to the Mu'tazila and his inclination towards their methods of investigation. He was invited to Egypt, so he responded to the invitation and traveled there, spreading his knowledge in Rajab 204 AH, at the age of fifty-four years. At the end of his life, may God have mercy on him, he was a scholar among scholars, unrivaled in his knowledge. Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said about him: It is narrated from the Prophet that God Almighty sends to this nation at the head of every hundred years a person who establishes for it its religious affairs. So 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz was at the head of the first hundred, and I hope that al-Shafi'i is at the head of the other hundred. He also said: Al-Shafi'i is a philosopher in four things: language, differences among people, meanings, and jurisprudence. And Dawud ibn 'Ali al-Zahiri said: Al-Shafi'i has virtues that have not been combined for anyone else: the nobility of his lineage, the soundness of his religion and creed, the generosity of his soul, his knowledge of the authentic and weak hadith, its abrogating and abrogated, his memorization of the Book and Sunnah and the biographies of the caliphs, and his excellence in composition. Throughout his life's journey, Imam al-Shafi'i moved between different countries and many circumstances. He acquired knowledge, jurisprudence, and shar'i investigations from diverse schools and from many teachers with multiple methodologies. He witnessed the conflict and dispute that took place at that time between the school of hadith and the school of opinion, and he became skilled in argumentation and debate until he became a debater of the highest order. He participated in the debates that took place between the scholars of the two schools; he would argue with the people of Iraq due to his knowledge of the Noble Quran and the Sunnah and their eloquence, and he would debate with the people of the Hijaz due to his understanding of legal rulings and analogical causes. He never debated anyone without prevailing. He used to benefit from the Hajj season during his residence in Mecca and his coming to it to meet with senior scholars in creed, hadith, jurisprudence, and language, taking from them and they from him, and he would argue and debate with them. Thus were combined in him soundness of mind, breadth of knowledge, eloquence of tongue, strength of expression, and solidity of style. Al-Shafi'i excelled in argumentation and debate until he surpassed his peers among the scholars of his time. He debated his teacher Muhammad ibn al-Hasan on many issues, and he had...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Shafi'i's life, focusing on his travels, education, and his exceptional skill in jadal (dialectical argumentation). The text first describes his return to Mecca and his teaching in the Haram, where he met Ahmad ibn Hanbal and taught for nine years. It then recounts his second trip to Baghdad and his subsequent move to Egypt, where he died at age fifty-four. The author then quotes two prominent scholars praising al-Shafi'i: Ahmad ibn Hanbal likens him to the reviver of religion at the turn of the century, and Dawud al-Zahiri lists his unmatched virtues. The passage then elaborates on al-Shafi'i's versatility in debate: he engaged scholars from both the hadith and opinion schools, arguing with Iraqis using Quran and Sunnah, and with Hijazis using legal reasoning and analogical causes. The text emphasizes his comprehensive mastery: he combined intellect, knowledge, eloquence, and style, surpassing his contemporaries. A specific example mentioned is his debates with his own teacher Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. The passage underscores that al-Shafi'i's jadal prowess was rooted in his diverse education and exposure to different methodologies.

Key Terms
الجدل
المناظرة
العلل القياسية

B) The Persian dominance and al-Ma'mun's favor towards the Mu'tazila made his stay uncomfortable.
C) He wanted to perform Hajj from Egypt.
D) He was exiled by the Caliph.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's biography reveals that his jadal mastery was built upon a foundation of diverse intellectual exposure and personal encounters with leading scholars of his time.

intermediate

Al-Shafi'i's Mastery of Jadal
Account of al-Shafi'i's debating skill and versatility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Shafi'i was able to debate effectively against both ahl al-hadith and ahl al-ra'y, and identify the two complementary strategies he used.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i debated Iraqis with Quran and Sunnah, and Hijazis with qiyas – he mastered both tools.

This passage highlights al-Shafi'i's exceptional skill in jadal (dialectical argumentation), showing how he could engage scholars from the hadith school and the ra'y school on their own terms. His success came from a rare combination of textual mastery and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing schools mentioned
The passage refers to 'the school of hadith' and 'the school of opinion' (ra'y). Recognize that these represent the two major approaches to Islamic law at the time.
2
Extract al-Shafi'i's debating strategies for each
Against Iraqis (who favored ra'y), he used Quran and Sunnah. Against Hijazis (who relied on hadith), he used legal rulings and analogical causes (al-'ilal al-qiyasiyyah).
3
Explain the effectiveness of each strategy
He could argue with Iraqis on their own ground by citing texts, which they also respected but often prioritized reason; and with Hijazis by demonstrating his grasp of qiyas, which they used but he mastered more deeply.
4
Note the result and the praise from contemporaries
He never debated anyone without prevailing. Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Dawud al-Zahiri praised his comprehensive knowledge, affirming that his jadal was not superficial but rooted in deep learning.

Source Text

Al-Shafi'i's Ethical Approach to Jadal
Describes al-Shafi'i's skill in jadal, his teachers, and his ethical approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ethical principles of jadal (dialectical debate) as exemplified by Imam al-Shafi'i and distinguish them from debate aimed at victory.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i's debates sought truth, not victory—a model for all Islamic discourse.

This passage describes not only al-Shafi'i's mastery of jadal but, more importantly, his ethical approach. He did not debate to win but to let truth emerge, even if it came from his opponent. This sets a high standard for Islamic scholarly exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Shafi'i's intellectual virtues
From the passage, list the domains of knowledge in which al-Shafi'i excelled (language, differences among people, meanings, jurisprudence) and the specific virtues mentioned by Dawud al-Zahiri (lineage, religion, generosity, hadith knowledge, etc.).
2
Analyze his debate success
Note that he debated both Iraqis (using Qur'an and Sunnah) and Hijazis (using legal rulings and analogical causes) and never lost. Consider how his comprehensive knowledge contributed to this.
3
Extract the core ethical principle from his quote
Read his statement: 'I have never debated anyone except that I loved that he be guided... I did not care whether God made the truth appear on my tongue or his tongue.' This shows his goal is truth, not personal victory.
4
Interpret the poem's advice on debate etiquette
The poem advises calmness, forbearance, avoiding obstinacy and boasting, and benefiting from the opponent's points. Identify these elements and relate them to al-Shafi'i's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقول أيضًا: «الشافعي فيلسوف في أربعة أشياء في اللغة واختلاف الناس والمعاني والفقه»(1) ويقول داود بن علي الظاهري (2): «للشافعي من الفضائل ما لم يجتمع لغيره من شرف نسبه وصحة دينه ومعتقده وسخاوة نفسه ومعرفته بصحة الحديث وسقيمه وناسخه ومنسوخه، وحفظ الكتاب والسنة وسيرة الخلفاء، وحسن التصنيف (3) وخلال رحلة حياته؛ تقلب الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه بين بلدان مختلفة وأحوال كثيرة، وأخذ العلم والفقه ومباحث الشريعة من مدارس متنوعة وعن شيوخ كثيرين متعددي المناهج، وقد عايش ما قام في ذلك العهد من صراع ونزاع بين مدرسة الحديث ومدرسة الرأي، وتمرس بالجدل والمناظرة حتى أصبح مناظرًا من الطراز الأول، فشارك في المناظرات التي قامت بين علماء المدرستين فكان يجادل أهل العراق لإلمامه بالقرآن الكريم والسنة وبلاغتها، ويناظر أهل الحجاز لإدراكه الحكم الشرعية والعلل القياسية ولم يناظر أحدا إلا ظهر عليه، وكان يستفيد من موسم الحج أثناء إقامته في مكة وقدومه إليها ليجتمع مع كبار العلماء في العقيدة والحديث والفقه واللغة فيأخذ منهم ويأخذون منه، ويجادلهم ويناظرهم، فاجتمع فيه رجاحة العقل وسعة الاطلاع، وفصاحة اللسان، وقوة البيان، ورصانة الأسلوب وقد برع الشافعي في الجدل والمناظرة حتى فاق فيها أقرانه من العلماء في عصره، فقد ناظر أستاذه محمد بن الحسن في كثير من المسائل كما كانت له مناظرات مع إسحاق بن راهويه، وأحمد بن حنبل وغيرهم. ولم يكن الشافعي في مناظراته طالب زعامة أو حب ظهور، وإنما كان مناظرا حسن المناظرة، أمينًا فيها طالبًا للحق منها، وقد بلغ من ذلك أن أثرت عنه هذه الكلمة: ما ناظرت أحدًا قط إلا أحببت أن يوفق ويسدد ويعان، وتكون عليه رعاية الله وحفظه، وما ناظرت أحدا إلا ولم أبال بين الله الحق على لساني أو من لسانه». وقد روى الربيع بن سليمان أن الشافعي كتب أبياتا إلى أبي يعقوب البويطي حنا له على الإنصاف والاتصاف بالأخلاق الحميدة في المناظرة، والأبيات هي: إذا كنت ذا فضل وعلم بما اختلف الأوائل والأواخر فناظر من تناظر في سكون حليماً لا تلج ولا تكابر يفيدك ما استفاد بلا امتنان من النكت اللطيفة والنوادر وإياك اللجوج ومن يرائي بأني قد غلبت ومن يفاخر
He also says: 'Al-Shafi'i is a philosopher in four things: in language, the differences among people, meanings, and jurisprudence.' And Dawud ibn Ali al-Zahiri says: 'Al-Shafi'i has virtues that have not been combined for anyone else: nobility of lineage, soundness of religion and belief, generosity of soul, knowledge of the authenticity and weakness of hadith, its abrogating and abrogated, memorization of the Book and the Sunnah and the biography of the caliphs, and excellence in authorship.' During his life journey, Imam al-Shafi'i, may God be pleased with him, moved between different countries and many conditions, and took knowledge, jurisprudence, and legal inquiries from diverse schools and from many teachers with multiple methodologies. He witnessed the conflict and dispute between the school of hadith and the school of opinion, and he practiced jadal and munazara until he became a debater of the first rank. He participated in the debates between the scholars of the two schools, debating the people of Iraq due to his knowledge of the Qur'an, the Sunnah, and its eloquence, and debating the people of Hijaz due to his understanding of legal rulings and analogical causes. He never debated anyone except that he prevailed. He used to benefit from the Hajj season during his stay in Mecca and his arrival there to meet with senior scholars in creed, hadith, jurisprudence, and language, taking from them and they from him, and debating with them. Thus, soundness of intellect, breadth of knowledge, eloquence of tongue, strength of expression, and solidity of style were combined in him. Al-Shafi'i excelled in jadal and munazara until he surpassed his peers among the scholars of his time. He debated his teacher Muhammad ibn al-Hasan on many issues, and he also had debates with Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and others. In his debates, al-Shafi'i was not seeking leadership or love of fame; rather, he was a good debater, trustworthy in it, seeking the truth through it. This reached such a level that this saying is attributed to him: 'I have never debated anyone except that I loved that he be guided, assisted, and helped, and that God's care and protection be upon him. I have never debated anyone except that I did not care whether God made the truth appear on my tongue or his tongue.' And al-Rabi' ibn Sulayman narrated that al-Shafi'i wrote verses to Abu Ya'qub al-Buwayti advising him on fairness and possessing good character in debate. The verses are: 'If you possess virtue and knowledge of what the earlier and later generations differed over, then debate with whoever you debate in calmness, as a forbearing person, not obstinate nor domineering. He benefits you from what he gains without gratitude, from subtle points and rare gems. Beware of the obstinate and the one who shows off, saying 'I have prevailed,' and the one who boasts.'
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological exposition of Imam al-Shafi'i's approach to jadal (dialectics) and munazara (debate). The author begins by quoting a statement that al-Shafi'i is a philosopher in four domains: language, differences among people, meanings, and jurisprudence. Then Dawud al-Zahiri lists al-Shafi'i's virtues, including his lineage, religious integrity, generosity, knowledge of hadith (authentic and weak, abrogating and abrogated), memorization of the Qur'an and Sunnah, and skill in authorship. The passage then describes al-Shafi'i's life journey, his exposure to different scholarly circles, and his role in the conflict between the school of hadith (ahl al-hadith) and the school of opinion (ahl al-ra'y). He mastered jadal and became a premier debater, able to argue with Iraqis using his knowledge of the Qur'an and Sunnah and with Hijazis using his understanding of legal rulings and analogical causation. He never lost a debate. During Hajj, he would meet with scholars from various fields and engage in mutual learning and debate. The text highlights that he combined sound intellect, vast knowledge, eloquence, strong expression, and refined style. He debated even his teacher Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, as well as Ishaq ibn Rahawayh and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Importantly, the passage emphasizes that al-Shafi'i did not seek fame or victory; he sought truth. He famously said that he wished his opponent to be guided and that he did not care whether truth came through his own tongue or his opponent's. This reflects the ideal adab of jadal: seeking truth, not superiority. Finally, the passage includes a poem by al-Shafi'i advising Abu Ya'qub al-Buwayti on debate etiquette: be calm, forbearing, not obstinate or domineering; benefit from the opponent's points; and avoid showing off or boasting about victory.

Key Terms
الجدل
المناظرة
الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To be defeated and humiliated.
B) To be guided, assisted, and protected by God.
C) To remain silent and listen only.
D) To concede that al-Shafi'i was correct.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's approach to jadal emphasizes that the ultimate goal is truth, and the debater should wish well for the opponent, maintaining calmness and avoiding arrogance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Based on al-Shafi'i's quoted statement, write a brief response to a debate opponent who is trying to belittle you. How would you remind yourself (and them) of the true purpose of jadal?
?

Dialectical Features of al-Shafi'i's Risala
Abd al-Raziq's analysis of the dialectical character of al-Risala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three dialectical manifestations in al-Shafi'i's Risala as described by Mustafa Abd al-Raziq.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i's Risala is a dialectical work blending logic, definition, and debate.

Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq observed that al-Shafi'i's Risala contains more than legal theory—it displays a distinctive dialectical method. This lesson unpacks his analysis, highlighting three key manifestations: the use of definitions and divisions, a dialogical style reminiscent of philosophy, and allusions to theological topics. Understanding these features will help you appreciate how dialectic (jadal) shaped early usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first manifestation: definitions and divisions
Find where Abd al-Raziq mentions al-Shafi'i's tendency to set down definitions (حدود) and then undertake divisions (تقسيم) with examples. Note how this logical structure serves dialectical comparison.
Al-Shafi'i sometimes presents multiple definitions and selects the soundest.
2
Recognize the second manifestation: dialectical dialogue
Look for the description of al-Shafi'i's 'dialectical dialogue saturated with the forms of logic' (الحوار الجدلي المشبع بصور المنطق). Notice the precision, refutation, and logical order that make it resemble philosophical dialogue.
This style relies primarily on transmitted sources (نقل) despite its philosophical appearance.
3
List the third manifestation: allusions to theology
Identify the topics Abd al-Raziq considers 'almost encroaching on theology' (تكاد تهجم على الإلهيات): knowledge, truth in apparent vs. hidden, mujtahid's error, Quran vs. Sunnah, causes of rulings, and authority of sources.
Al-Shafi'i's argument for the authority of the Sunnah also turns attention to the authority of the Quran itself.
4
Synthesize: how these manifestations show dialectic
Consider how each manifestation—definitions, dialogue, theological allusions—serves the dialectical purpose of establishing and defending legal principles through reasoned debate.
This anticipates later usul al-fiqh and kalam discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس هذا النص الذي ذكرناه هو المثال الوحيد للجدل الأصولي في أول مؤلف في هذا العلم، وإنما هو نموذج من نماذج كثيرة نجدها مبثوثة في ثنايا الكتاب. هذا، وقد لاحظ الشيخ مصطفى عبد الرازق هذا الطابع الجدلي الذي يغلب على (الرسالة)، فقال يصف منهج الإمام الشافعي في تأليفها : «إذا كنا نلمح في الرسالة نشأة التفكير الفلسفي في الإسلام من ناحية العناية بضبط الفروع والجزئيات بقواعد كلية وإن لم تغفل جانب الفقه . . فإننا نلمح للتفكير الفلسفي في الرسالة مظاهر أخرى: منها ؛ هذا الاتجاه المنطقي إلى وضع الحدود والتعاريف أولا، ثم الأخذ في التقسيم مع التمثيل والاستشهاد لكل قسم وقد يعرض الشافعي لسرد التعريفات المختلفة ليقارن بينها وينتهي به التمحيص إلى تخير ما يرتضيه منها . ومنها ؛ أسلوبه في الحوار الجدلي المشبع بصور المنطق ومعانيه، حتى لتكاد تحسبه لما فيه من دقة البحث ولطف الفهم وحسن التصرف في الاستدلال والنقض ومراعاة النظام المنطقي - حوارًا فلسفيًا، على رغم اعتماده على النقل أولا وبالذات واتصاله بأمور شرعية خالصة . . ومنها ؛ الإيماء إلى مباحث من علم الأصول تكاد تهجم على الإلهيات أو علم الكلام كالبحث في العلم وأن هناك حقا في الظاهر والباطن وحقا في الظاهر دون الباطن ، وأن المجتهد مصيب أو مخطئ معذور، والفرق بين القرآن والسنة، وعلل الأحكام، وترتيب الأصول بحسب قوتها وضعفها، وقد استدل الشافعي على حجية السنة وما دونها من الأصول، فلفت الأذهان إلى حجية القرآن نفسه، وهي مسألة وثيقة الاتصال بأبحاث المتكلمين». المطلب الثالث: الجدل الأصولي في الكتب الأخرى للشافعي. ليس كتاب (الرسالة) هو الكتاب الوحيد الذي أنشأه الشافعي في علم أصول الفقه، وكان يكتسي الطابع الجدلي، فإن له مؤلفات أخرى في هذا العلم لم يحد فيها عن منهجه الذي كتب به بحوث (الرسالة) . . فكتاب (جماع العلم)، ما هو إلا كتاب تطبيقي في الجدل الأصولي، إذ ذكر فيه الإمام الشافعي عدة مناظرات ومناقشات جرت بينه وبين بعض معاصريه حول مسائل من أصول الفقه المناظرة الأولى جرت بينه وبين بعض المنكرين للعمل بالأحاديث كلها، وهي مناظرة طويلة أخذت حيزًا لا بأس به من الكتاب والثانية جرت بينه وبين جماعة كانوا لا يرون حجية خبر الواحد، وهي مناظرة قصيرة أفضت إلى مناظرة ثالثة أكثر طولاً في شأن الإجماع وحقيقته وحجيته. وقد ألف الشافعي هذا الكتاب بعد كتاب (الرسالة)، وأحال فيه في بعض المواضع عليه ففصل في هذا بعض ما أجمل في (الرسالة)، وأجمل في هذا بعض ما فصل هناك. وأما كتاب إبطال الاستحسان فهو كذلك عبارة عن حوار جدلي استهدف منه الإمام الشافعي إبطال ما اشتهر الأحناف بدعوى العمل به في عصره، ألا وهو
And this text that we have mentioned is not the only example of dialectic in the first authored work in this science, but rather it is a model of many models that we find scattered throughout the book. This, and Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq observed this dialectical character that predominates in (al-Risala), and he said describing the method of Imam al-Shafi'i in composing it: 'If we glimpse in the Risala the emergence of philosophical thought in Islam from the aspect of attention to regulating branches and particulars by universal rules, although it did not neglect the side of jurisprudence... then we glimpse for philosophical thought in the Risala other manifestations: Among them: this logical tendency to set down definitions first, then to undertake division with examples and citations for each section, and al-Shafi'i might present different definitions to compare between them and examination leads him to choose what he approves of. Among them: his style in dialectical dialogue saturated with the forms of logic and its meanings, so that you would almost think it, due to its precision of investigation, subtlety of understanding, good conduct in inference and refutation, and observance of logical order, a philosophical dialogue, despite his reliance on transmission primarily and fundamentally and his connection to purely religious matters... Among them: alluding to topics from usul that almost encroach on theology or kalam, such as the investigation into knowledge and that there is truth in the apparent and the hidden, and truth in the apparent without the hidden, and that the mujtahid is correct or mistaken but excused, and the difference between Quran and Sunnah, and causes of rulings, and arrangement of principles according to their strength and weakness, and al-Shafi'i argued for the authority of the Sunnah and what is below it of principles, so he turned minds to the authority of the Quran itself, and it is a matter closely connected to the investigations of the theologians.' The third demand: Dialectic in the other books of al-Shafi'i. The book (al-Risala) is not the only book that al-Shafi'i authored in usul al-fiqh, and it acquired a dialectical character, for he has other works in this science in which he did not deviate from his method by which he wrote the researches of (al-Risala)... For the book (Jima' al-Ilm) is nothing but an applied book in dialectic, for Imam al-Shafi'i mentioned in it several debates and discussions that took place between him and some of his contemporaries concerning issues of usul al-fiqh. The first debate took place between him and some of those who denied acting upon hadiths altogether, and it is a long debate that took up a considerable space of the book. The second took place between him and a group who did not consider the authority of a single-narrator report (khabar al-wahid), and it is a short debate that led to a third debate, longer, concerning consensus (ijma'), its reality and authority. And al-Shafi'i authored this book after (al-Risala), and he referred in some places to it, so he detailed in this some of what he summarized in (al-Risala), and he summarized in this some of what he detailed there. As for the book (Ibtal al-Istihsan), it is likewise a dialectical dialogue aimed at refuting what the Hanafis were famous for claiming to act upon in his time, namely
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological discussion that highlights the dialectical nature of al-Shafi'i's works on usul al-fiqh. It begins by stating that the previous example (presumably from the Risala) is not unique; many examples are scattered throughout the book. Then it quotes Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq, who identifies several manifestations of philosophical thought in the Risala: first, a logical approach of setting definitions and then dividing with examples; second, a dialectical dialogue style that resembles philosophical discourse despite relying on transmitted sources; third, references to theological issues like knowledge, truth, and the authority of sources. The passage then introduces a third section on dialectic in al-Shafi'i's other books. It specifies that the Risala is not the only dialectical work; Jima' al-Ilm is applied dialectic, containing debates with opponents of hadith and of khabar al-wahid, leading to a debate on ijma'. Al-Shafi'i composed Jima' al-Ilm after the Risala, sometimes detailing what was summarized and vice versa. Finally, Ibtal al-Istihsan is described as a dialectical dialogue refuting the Hanafi practice of istihsan. The passage thus demonstrates that dialectic (jadal) was central to al-Shafi'i's method in usul, not just in the Risala but in his other major works.

جدل
أصول الفقه
حدود
تقسيم

Applied Dialectic in Jima' al-Ilm and Ibtal al-Istihsan
Description of dialectic in al-Shafi'i's other usul works: Jima' al-Ilm and Ibtal al-Istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the dialectical debates recorded in al-Shafi'i's Jima' al-Ilm and the purpose of Ibtal al-Istihsan as dialectical works.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i applied dialectic directly to refute opponents of hadith and other usul doctrines.

While al-Risala established the theoretical framework, al-Shafi'i's other works—Jima' al-Ilm and Ibtal al-Istihsan—are practical applications of dialectic. This lesson examines the specific debates al-Shafi'i engaged in, showing how he defended the authority of hadith, consensus, and rejected certain legal methods. Understanding these debates will ground your knowledge of how jadal was used in early usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dialectical nature of Jima' al-Ilm
Read the passage's description of Jima' al-Ilm as 'an applied book in dialectic' (كتاب تطبيقي في الجدل الأصولي). Note that it contains debates (مناظرات) between al-Shafi'i and his contemporaries.
The book is composed after al-Risala and sometimes details what was summarized there.
2
List the three debates in Jima' al-Ilm
Find the three debates mentioned: (1) with those denying acting upon hadiths altogether; (2) with those rejecting the authority of khabar al-wahid; (3) a longer debate on consensus (ijma'). Recognize each opponent's position.
The second debate is short and leads to the third.
3
Understand the dialectical purpose of Ibtal al-Istihsan
Note that Ibtal al-Istihsan is described as a 'dialectical dialogue' aimed at refuting the Hanafi practice of istihsan. Consider how this fits into al-Shafi'i's overall method of defending textual sources over personal opinion.
Istihsan was a key point of contention between al-Shafi'i and the Hanafis.
4
Compare theoretical vs. applied dialectic
Reflect on how Jima' al-Ilm and Ibtal al-Istihsan put into practice the dialectical style described in the Risala. They show that jadal was not just for theory but for actual argumentation against specific groups.
Al-Shafi'i's works together form a coherent dialectical project.

وليس هذا النص الذي ذكرناه هو المثال الوحيد للجدل الأصولي في أول مؤلف في هذا العلم، وإنما هو نموذج من نماذج كثيرة نجدها مبثوثة في ثنايا الكتاب. هذا، وقد لاحظ الشيخ مصطفى عبد الرازق هذا الطابع الجدلي الذي يغلب على (الرسالة)، فقال يصف منهج الإمام الشافعي في تأليفها : «إذا كنا نلمح في الرسالة نشأة التفكير الفلسفي في الإسلام من ناحية العناية بضبط الفروع والجزئيات بقواعد كلية وإن لم تغفل جانب الفقه . . فإننا نلمح للتفكير الفلسفي في الرسالة مظاهر أخرى: منها ؛ هذا الاتجاه المنطقي إلى وضع الحدود والتعاريف أولا، ثم الأخذ في التقسيم مع التمثيل والاستشهاد لكل قسم وقد يعرض الشافعي لسرد التعريفات المختلفة ليقارن بينها وينتهي به التمحيص إلى تخير ما يرتضيه منها . ومنها ؛ أسلوبه في الحوار الجدلي المشبع بصور المنطق ومعانيه، حتى لتكاد تحسبه لما فيه من دقة البحث ولطف الفهم وحسن التصرف في الاستدلال والنقض ومراعاة النظام المنطقي - حوارًا فلسفيًا، على رغم اعتماده على النقل أولا وبالذات واتصاله بأمور شرعية خالصة . . ومنها ؛ الإيماء إلى مباحث من علم الأصول تكاد تهجم على الإلهيات أو علم الكلام كالبحث في العلم وأن هناك حقا في الظاهر والباطن وحقا في الظاهر دون الباطن ، وأن المجتهد مصيب أو مخطئ معذور، والفرق بين القرآن والسنة، وعلل الأحكام، وترتيب الأصول بحسب قوتها وضعفها، وقد استدل الشافعي على حجية السنة وما دونها من الأصول، فلفت الأذهان إلى حجية القرآن نفسه، وهي مسألة وثيقة الاتصال بأبحاث المتكلمين». المطلب الثالث: الجدل الأصولي في الكتب الأخرى للشافعي. ليس كتاب (الرسالة) هو الكتاب الوحيد الذي أنشأه الشافعي في علم أصول الفقه، وكان يكتسي الطابع الجدلي، فإن له مؤلفات أخرى في هذا العلم لم يحد فيها عن منهجه الذي كتب به بحوث (الرسالة) . . فكتاب (جماع العلم)، ما هو إلا كتاب تطبيقي في الجدل الأصولي، إذ ذكر فيه الإمام الشافعي عدة مناظرات ومناقشات جرت بينه وبين بعض معاصريه حول مسائل من أصول الفقه المناظرة الأولى جرت بينه وبين بعض المنكرين للعمل بالأحاديث كلها، وهي مناظرة طويلة أخذت حيزًا لا بأس به من الكتاب والثانية جرت بينه وبين جماعة كانوا لا يرون حجية خبر الواحد، وهي مناظرة قصيرة أفضت إلى مناظرة ثالثة أكثر طولاً في شأن الإجماع وحقيقته وحجيته. وقد ألف الشافعي هذا الكتاب بعد كتاب (الرسالة)، وأحال فيه في بعض المواضع عليه ففصل في هذا بعض ما أجمل في (الرسالة)، وأجمل في هذا بعض ما فصل هناك. وأما كتاب إبطال الاستحسان فهو كذلك عبارة عن حوار جدلي استهدف منه الإمام الشافعي إبطال ما اشتهر الأحناف بدعوى العمل به في عصره، ألا وهو
And this text that we have mentioned is not the only example of dialectic in the first authored work in this science, but rather it is a model of many models that we find scattered throughout the book. This, and Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq observed this dialectical character that predominates in (al-Risala), and he said describing the method of Imam al-Shafi'i in composing it: 'If we glimpse in the Risala the emergence of philosophical thought in Islam from the aspect of attention to regulating branches and particulars by universal rules, although it did not neglect the side of jurisprudence... then we glimpse for philosophical thought in the Risala other manifestations: Among them: this logical tendency to set down definitions first, then to undertake division with examples and citations for each section, and al-Shafi'i might present different definitions to compare between them and examination leads him to choose what he approves of. Among them: his style in dialectical dialogue saturated with the forms of logic and its meanings, so that you would almost think it, due to its precision of investigation, subtlety of understanding, good conduct in inference and refutation, and observance of logical order, a philosophical dialogue, despite his reliance on transmission primarily and fundamentally and his connection to purely religious matters... Among them: alluding to topics from usul that almost encroach on theology or kalam, such as the investigation into knowledge and that there is truth in the apparent and the hidden, and truth in the apparent without the hidden, and that the mujtahid is correct or mistaken but excused, and the difference between Quran and Sunnah, and causes of rulings, and arrangement of principles according to their strength and weakness, and al-Shafi'i argued for the authority of the Sunnah and what is below it of principles, so he turned minds to the authority of the Quran itself, and it is a matter closely connected to the investigations of the theologians.' The third demand: Dialectic in the other books of al-Shafi'i. The book (al-Risala) is not the only book that al-Shafi'i authored in usul al-fiqh, and it acquired a dialectical character, for he has other works in this science in which he did not deviate from his method by which he wrote the researches of (al-Risala)... For the book (Jima' al-Ilm) is nothing but an applied book in dialectic, for Imam al-Shafi'i mentioned in it several debates and discussions that took place between him and some of his contemporaries concerning issues of usul al-fiqh. The first debate took place between him and some of those who denied acting upon hadiths altogether, and it is a long debate that took up a considerable space of the book. The second took place between him and a group who did not consider the authority of a single-narrator report (khabar al-wahid), and it is a short debate that led to a third debate, longer, concerning consensus (ijma'), its reality and authority. And al-Shafi'i authored this book after (al-Risala), and he referred in some places to it, so he detailed in this some of what he summarized in (al-Risala), and he summarized in this some of what he detailed there. As for the book (Ibtal al-Istihsan), it is likewise a dialectical dialogue aimed at refuting what the Hanafis were famous for claiming to act upon in his time, namely
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological discussion that highlights the dialectical nature of al-Shafi'i's works on usul al-fiqh. It begins by stating that the previous example (presumably from the Risala) is not unique; many examples are scattered throughout the book. Then it quotes Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq, who identifies several manifestations of philosophical thought in the Risala: first, a logical approach of setting definitions and then dividing with examples; second, a dialectical dialogue style that resembles philosophical discourse despite relying on transmitted sources; third, references to theological issues like knowledge, truth, and the authority of sources. The passage then introduces a third section on dialectic in al-Shafi'i's other books. It specifies that the Risala is not the only dialectical work; Jima' al-Ilm is applied dialectic, containing debates with opponents of hadith and of khabar al-wahid, leading to a debate on ijma'. Al-Shafi'i composed Jima' al-Ilm after the Risala, sometimes detailing what was summarized and vice versa. Finally, Ibtal al-Istihsan is described as a dialectical dialogue refuting the Hanafi practice of istihsan. The passage thus demonstrates that dialectic (jadal) was central to al-Shafi'i's method in usul, not just in the Risala but in his other major works.

Al-Shafi'i's Dialectical Methodology in Usul
Describes al-Shafi'i's dialectical works beyond al-Risala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Shafi'i's dialectical method in his usul works and distinguish the two types of istihsan he addressed.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i's usul works are fundamentally dialectical engagements, not mere monologues.

Al-Shafi'i is famous for al-Risala, but his other usul works are equally important and deeply dialectical. In Jami' al-'Ilm and Ibtal al-Istihsan, he engages with opponents through structured debates. Understanding this dialectical approach is crucial for grasping how early usul al-fiqh was forged through intellectual confrontation. In this lesson, we'll explore the debates and clarify a key distinction about istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dialectical works
The passage lists Jami' al-'Ilm and Ibtal al-Istihsan as dialectical works. Note that they were written after al-Risala and complement it. Jami' al-'Ilm contains recorded debates; Ibtal al-Istihsan is a question-and-answer dialogue.
2
Analyze the debates in Jami' al-'Ilm
Three debates are mentioned: (1) against those rejecting all hadith, (2) against those denying khabar al-wahid, and (3) an extended discussion on ijma'. Each debate addresses a foundational usul issue.
These debates show al-Shafi'i defending the authority of hadith and consensus.
3
Distinguish the two types of istihsan
The passage explicitly clarifies that al-Shafi'i did not reject all istihsan, only the arbitrary kind based on personal whim without evidence. The legitimate istihsan (based on Quran, Sunna, ijma', or maslaha) was accepted by al-Shafi'i himself.
This distinction is crucial to avoid misunderstanding al-Shafi'i's position.
4
Connect fiqh works to usul methodology
The passage notes that al-Shafi'i's fiqh works like al-Umm and Ahkam al-Quran are also dialectical and reflect his usul methodology. They are applied usul, showing theory in practice.
Thus, usul is not separate from fiqh; it is the backbone of juristic reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثالث: الجدل الأصولي في الكتب الأخرى للشافعي
ليس كتاب (الرسالة) هو الكتاب الوحيد الذي أنشأه الشافعي في علم أصول الفقه، وكان يكتسي الطابع الجدلي، فإن له مؤلفات أخرى في هذا العلم لم يحد فيها عن منهجه الذي كتب به بحوث (الرسالة) . . فكتاب (جماع العلم)، ما هو إلا كتاب تطبيقي في الجدل الأصولي، إذ ذكر فيه الإمام الشافعي عدة مناظرات ومناقشات جرت بينه وبين بعض معاصريه حول مسائل من أصول الفقه المناظرة الأولى جرت بينه وبين بعض المنكرين للعمل بالأحاديث كلها، وهي مناظرة طويلة أخذت حيزًا لا بأس به من الكتاب والثانية جرت بينه وبين جماعة كانوا لا يرون حجية خبر الواحد، وهي مناظرة قصيرة أفضت إلى مناظرة ثالثة أكثر طولاً في شأن الإجماع وحقيقته وحجيته وقد ألف الشافعي هذا الكتاب بعد كتاب (الرسالة)، وأحال فيه في بعض المواضع عليه ففصل في هذا بعض ما أجمل في (الرسالة)، وأجمل في هذا بعض ما فصل هناك وأما كتاب إبطال الاستحسان فهو كذلك عبارة عن حوار جدلي استهدف منه الإمام الشافعي إبطال ما اشتهر الأحناف بدعوى العمل به في عصره، ألا وهو (الاستحسان)، فقد ألف الشافعي هذا الكتاب لما رأى كثرة هروبهم إلى الاستحسان حين تعوزهم الأدلة للاحتجاج بها لمذهبهم، فيقولون: نحن نستحسن، وقد اجتهد الشافعي في إبطال هذا الاستحسان بمناقشة جزئيات في حوار علمي أداره في شكل سؤال وجواب بينه وبين مخالف أو معترض مفترض لكن ربما كان من الجدير بالذكر هنا، ودفعا لأي التباس أن الاستحسان الذي أبطله الشافعي في هذا الكتاب ليس هو الاستحسان الأصولي المعروف الذي يعمل به الشافعي نفسه، وإنما هو الاستحسان الذي يخضع لهوى المستدل ولا يستند إلى أي دليل من كتاب أو سنة أو إجماع أو مصلحة راجحة. وليست هذه الكتب المذكورة هي فقط التراث الأصولي للإمام الشافعي، بل إن الدارس لمؤلفاته الفقهية الأخرى مثل كتاب (الأم)، وكتاب (أحكام القرآن) يلمس بوضوح منهجه العلمي في تحليل النصوص وعرض المسائل بطريقة أصولية - منحاه الاجتهادي، فكتبه الفقهية هي كتب في أصول الفقه التطبيقي جدلية تكشف عن منحاه الاجتهادي
The third demand: Al-Usuli Dialectic in al-Shafi'i's Other Books. Al-Risala is not the only book that al-Shafi'i authored in the science of usul al-fiqh, and it bore a dialectical character. For he has other works in this science in which he did not deviate from the methodology with which he wrote the researches of al-Risala. Thus, the book Jami' al-'Ilm is nothing but an applied work in usuli dialectic, for Imam al-Shafi'i mentioned in it several debates and discussions that took place between him and some of his contemporaries on issues of usul al-fiqh. The first debate took place between him and some of those who denied acting upon hadith altogether, and it is a lengthy debate that took up a considerable portion of the book. The second occurred between him and a group who did not consider the solitary report (khabar al-wahid) as authoritative, and it is a short debate that led to a third, more lengthy debate concerning consensus (ijma') and its reality and authority. Al-Shafi'i authored this book after al-Risala, and referred to it in some places, thus detailing in this some of what was summarized in al-Risala, and summarizing in this some of what was detailed there. As for the book Ibtal al-Istihsan (Refuting Istihsan), it is likewise a dialectical dialogue aimed by Imam al-Shafi'i at refuting what the Hanafis were famous for claiming to act upon in his time, namely istihsan. For al-Shafi'i authored this book when he saw their frequent flight to istihsan when evidence failed them to argue for their school, saying: 'We find it good (nastahsin).' Al-Shafi'i exerted effort in refuting this istihsan by discussing particulars in a scholarly dialogue he conducted in the form of question and answer between himself and an assumed opponent or objector. But it might be worth mentioning here, to avoid any confusion, that the istihsan which al-Shafi'i refuted in this book is not the well-known usuli istihsan that al-Shafi'i himself practices, but rather the istihsan that submits to the whim of the reasoner and does not rely on any evidence from the Book, Sunna, consensus, or a preponderant interest. These mentioned books are not the only usuli legacy of Imam al-Shafi'i; rather, the student of his other jurisprudential works, such as the book al-Umm and the book Ahkam al-Quran, clearly perceives his scientific methodology in analyzing texts and presenting issues in a usuli manner—his ijtihad approach. For his fiqh books are books of applied usul al-fiqh, dialectical, revealing his ijtihad approach.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly description of Imam al-Shafi'i's works on usul al-fiqh beyond his famous al-Risala, emphasizing their dialectical (jadal) nature. The author begins by stating that al-Risala is not alone in bearing a dialectical character; al-Shafi'i's other works follow the same methodology. The first work discussed is Jami' al-'Ilm, described as a practical application of usuli dialectic. It contains three recorded debates: the first with those who reject all hadith, the second with those who deny the authority of solitary reports (khabar al-wahid), and a third, more extensive debate on consensus (ijma'). The passage notes that Jami' al-'Ilm was written after al-Risala, and the two works complement each other in level of detail. The second work is Ibtal al-Istihsan, a polemical dialogue targeting the Hanafi practice of istihsan (juristic preference). Al-Shafi'i wrote it because he observed that Hanafis frequently resorted to istihsan when lacking scriptural evidence. The author clarifies a crucial point: the istihsan al-Shafi'i refuted is not the legitimate usuli istihsan that he himself sometimes employed, but rather a capricious preference unsupported by any textual or rational evidence. The passage concludes by noting that even al-Shafi'i's purely fiqh works, like al-Umm and Ahkam al-Quran, are methodologically usuli and dialectical, revealing his ijtihad approach. This description highlights the centrality of dialectical engagement in the formation of usul al-fiqh.

الاستحسان

Al-Shafi'i's Rejection of Istihsan: Distinguishing Two Meanings
Author explains al-Shafi'i's critique of istihsan and clarifies its meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the istihsan al-Shafi'i rejected and the usuli istihsan he accepted.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i did not reject all istihsan, only the arbitrary one without evidence.

This passage explains that al-Shafi'i wrote his book to counter jurists who used istihsan as a fallback when evidence was lacking. The author emphasizes that the istihsan al-Shafi'i rejected is not the same as the well-known usuli principle that al-Shafi'i himself used. Understanding this distinction is crucial to avoid a common misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reason for al-Shafi'i's book
The passage states al-Shafi'i saw many jurists resorting to istihsan when evidence failed them. They would simply say 'we seek istihsan'. This prompted him to write a book refuting this practice.
2
Recognize the method of refutation
Al-Shafi'i discussed specific cases in a question-and-answer dialogue with an imaginary opponent or objector. This shows his systematic approach.
This is a dialectical method, but the passage only mentions it in passing.
3
Distinguish between two types of istihsan
The author explicitly warns: the istihsan al-Shafi'i refuted is not the well-known usuli principle that he himself practiced. The rejected one is based on personal whim without any evidence from the Qur'an, Sunna, consensus, or preponderant interest.
This is the core analytical move.
4
Apply the distinction
When encountering a claim that al-Shafi'i rejected istihsan entirely, check which meaning is intended. Use the criteria: is it evidence-based or arbitrary?
This guards against conflating homonymous terms in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(الاستحسان)، فقد ألف الشافعي هذا الكتاب لما رأى كثرة هروبهم إلى الاستحسان حين تعوزهم الأدلة للاحتجاج بها لمذهبهم، فيقولون: نحن نستحسن، وقد اجتهد الشافعي في إبطال هذا الاستحسان بمناقشة جزئيات في حوار علمي أداره في شكل سؤال وجواب بينه وبين مخالف أو معترض مفترض (1) لكن ربما كان من الجدير بالذكر هنا، ودفعا لأي التباس أن الاستحسان الذي أبطله الشافعي في هذا الكتاب ليس هو الاستحسان الأصولي المعروف الذي يعمل به الشافعي نفسه، وإنما هو الاستحسان الذي يخضع لهوى المستدل ولا يستند إلى أي دليل من كتاب أو سنة أو إجماع أو مصلحة راجحة (2).
Regarding istihsan: Al-Shafi'i authored this book when he saw their frequent resort to istihsan when evidence failed them to argue for their school, saying: 'We seek istihsan.' He exerted effort in refuting this istihsan by discussing particulars in a scholarly dialogue he conducted in question-and-answer form between himself and an opponent or a hypothetical objector. But perhaps it is worth mentioning here, and to avoid any confusion, that the istihsan which al-Shafi'i refuted in this book is not the well-known usuli istihsan that al-Shafi'i himself practices, but rather the istihsan that follows the whim of the reasoner and is not based on any evidence from the Book, Sunna, consensus, or preponderant interest.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage clarifies al-Shafi'i's stance on istihsan. It begins by stating that al-Shafi'i wrote this particular book because he observed many jurists resorting to istihsan whenever they lacked textual evidence to support their school. They would simply say: 'We seek istihsan.' Al-Shafi'i responded by systematically discussing specific cases in a dialectical format, presenting questions and answers between himself and an imagined opponent or objector. The author then emphasises a crucial distinction: the istihsan al-Shafi'i refuted here is not the well-known usuli principle of istihsan that al-Shafi'i himself accepted and employed in his own rulings. Rather, it is a subjective form of istihsan driven by personal desire, without any basis in the Qur'an, Sunna, consensus, or a preponderant maslaha. This guards against conflating two different concepts under the same term.

B) The istihsan that follows the reasoner's whim without any evidence

D) The istihsan that contradicts explicit Qur'anic texts

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i rejected only arbitrary istihsan without evidence; the usuli istihsan based on stronger evidence is a valid source of law accepted by him.

Development of Jadal in Usul al-Fiqh After al-Shafi'i
Author describes the growth of jadal in usul al-fiqh and the division of scholars regarding al-Shafi'i's Risala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two scholarly factions that emerged in response to al-Shafi'i's Risala and explain how each engaged with it.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i's Risala sparked both a movement and a counter-movement in usul al-fiqh.

This passage traces how al-Shafi'i's Risala became the catalyst for the development of jadal (dialectic) in usul al-fiqh. However, not all scholars welcomed it. Understanding this division is key to grasping the dynamic nature of early Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impetus
Look for what al-Shafi'i provided that sparked development: rules and principles for legal reasoning and ijtihad.
The Risala served as a foundation for usul studies.
2
Recognize the captivation
Note which scholars were drawn to his method and why: those engaged in creedal issues, because it matched their rational inclinations.
Al-Shafi'i's dialectical method appealed to mutakallimun as well.
3
Note the expansion
Observe how scholars expanded usul: they wrote many works and broadened research and debate.
This led to innovation in the subject of usul.
4
Pinpoint the division
Identify the two groups: the people of hadith who accepted the Risala, and the people of opinion who rejected most of it and sought to refute it.
The division was based on adherence to hadith vs. personal opinion.
5
Connect to later history
Consider how this division influenced later usul works: the Risala became a central reference for one school and a target for another.
This tension drove further development in jadal.

المطلب الرابع : تطور الجدل الأصولي بعد الشافعي بعد الشافعي رحمه الله ، بدأ التطور الفعلي للدراسات الأصولية، فهو، رضي الله عنه قد أعطى دفعة قوية لهذه الدراسات بما استطاع أن يجمعه من قواعد وقوانين للاستدلال والاجتهاد الفقهي وما تركه من انطباع شجع العلماء من بعده (1) على ارتياد ميدان الدراسات الأصولية، انطلاقا من الرسالة التي تم الاستهداء بها في الدراسات الجديدة . ومع بدء التطور الفعلي للدراسة الأصولية، بدأ أيضًا التطور الفعلي للجدل في أصول الفقه، فقد استهوى المنهج العلمي الجدلي للإمام الشافعي الكثير من العلماء، وخاصة المشتغلين منهم بقضايا العقيدة إذ أنه يتمشى مع ميولهم العقلية وطرقهم النظرية الاستدلالية، فوجدوا فيه مجالاً لإشباع اتجاهاتهم العلمية، فأبدعوا في تطوير علم الأصول ،موضوعًا، وأكثروا من التأليف فيه، وأوسعوا مجال البحث والجدل في قضاياه، فنهض بذلك أعلامهم وأئمتهم وهكذا سيطرة رسالة الشافعي منذ ظهورها على الدراسات الأصولية، لكن الذي حدث أن العلماء لم يتفقوا على رأي واحد في شأنها، فقد انقسموا إلى فريقين : فريق تقبل الرسالة وحولها إلى قاعدة حجاج عن مذهبه، وهم جمهور أهل الحديث، وفريق رفض معظم ما جاء فيها وأدرك أن عليه أن يرد على صاحبها ما أورده مما يخالف مذهبه قبل أن يتأثر الناس بما جاء فيها، وهذا ينطبق على جمهور أهل الرأي والمخالفين في الأمور التي تعرض لها الإمام في رسالته .
Fourth Topic: The Development of Jadal in Usul after al-Shafi'i. After al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, the actual development of usul studies began. He, may Allah be pleased with him, gave a strong impetus to these studies by what he compiled of rules and principles for legal reasoning and ijtihad, and by the impression he left that encouraged scholars after him to venture into the field of usul studies, starting from the Risala which was used as a guide in the new studies. With the beginning of the actual development of usul study, the actual development of jadal in usul al-fiqh also began. The scientific dialectical method of al-Shafi'i captivated many scholars, especially those engaged in issues of creed, as it matched their rational inclinations and theoretical methods of reasoning. They found in it a field to satisfy their scientific tendencies, so they innovated in developing the subject of usul, wrote many works on it, and expanded the scope of research and debate in its issues. Thus their prominent figures and imams advanced it. And thus al-Shafi'i's Risala dominated usul studies since its appearance, but what happened was that scholars did not agree on a single opinion regarding it; they split into two groups: a group that accepted the Risala and made it a foundation for arguing for their school, and they are the majority of the people of hadith; and a group that rejected most of what was in it and realized that they had to respond to its author regarding what he had presented that contradicted their school, before people were influenced by what it contained, and this applies to the majority of the people of opinion and those who disagreed in matters that the Imam addressed in his Risala.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage outlines the historical development of jadal (dialectic) within usul al-fiqh after al-Shafi'i. It begins by stating that actual progress in usul studies started after al-Shafi'i, thanks to his compilation of legal rules and principles. His intellectual impact encouraged subsequent scholars to delve into usul. The author then specifically notes that jadal in usul al-fiqh began to develop as well. Al-Shafi'i's dialectical methodology attracted many scholars, particularly those involved in theological issues (kalam), because it suited their rational dispositions and deductive reasoning. They found in his method a means to pursue their scientific interests, leading to innovations in the field, prolific writing, and expansion of debate. However, the author highlights a crucial division: scholars did not unanimously accept al-Shafi'i's Risala. They split into two factions. The first—mainly the adherents of hadith—accepted the Risala and used it as a basis for arguing their school. The second—mainly the adherents of personal opinion (ahl al-ra'y) and those who differed with al-Shafi'i on specific issues—rejected most of its content and felt compelled to refute him before his views could influence others. This passage thus explains both the progressive impact and the contentious reception of al-Shafi'i's work.

Key Terms
الجدل (al-jadal): In this context, the dialectical method of argumentation used in usul al-fiqh, inspired by al-Shafi'i's approach in his Risala. [Note: This term has a wider usage in mantiq; here it refers specifically to the methodological debate in fiqh and usul.]
الرسالة (al-Risala): Al-Shafi'i's foundational work on usul al-fiqh, which became a central reference and subject of debate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group of scholars primarily accepted al-Shafi'i's Risala and made it a basis for their arguments?
A) The people of opinion (ahl al-ra'y)
B) The people of hadith (ahl al-hadith)
C) The Mu'tazilites
D) The Sufis

Key Takeaway
The reception of al-Shafi'i's Risala was not unanimous; it created a division that spurred further development in usul al-fiqh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: In your own words, explain why the people of hadith accepted al-Shafi'i's Risala while the people of opinion rejected it. Use evidence from the passage.
?
Task 2: Identify a modern-day legal debate in Islamic jurisprudence (e.g., riba, hijab) and consider how the dialectical method of jadal could be applied to structure arguments for and against a particular ruling.

Early Usul Scholars and Their Works
Lists Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki scholars with their major usul works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key early usul scholars from the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki schools and their major works, and explain the motivation behind these works in the context of the development of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Early usul works were often written to defend a madhhab's methodology against rivals.

Many students of usul al-fiqh are familiar with later comprehensive works, but the early formative period saw a flurry of authorship driven by inter-madhhab debate and the need to systematize legal principles. This lesson surveys the first generations of usul authors across the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki schools, as listed in our source passage, and explores why these works were composed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three madhhabs mentioned
The passage covers scholars from the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki schools. Notice how the text groups them: first the Hanafis, then the Shafi'is, then the Malikis.
2
List scholars and works per madhhab
For each madhhab, extract the names of scholars and their specific books. For example, Hanafis include 'Isa ibn Aban (Khabar al-Wahid, Ithbat al-Qiyas), al-Maturidi (Ma'akhidh al-Shara'i'), and al-Jassas (Usul al-Karkhi wa al-Jassas).
Some works are described briefly; pay attention to the titles and authors.
3
Note the stated motivations
The passage explicitly says the Hanafis studied al-Shafi'i's Risala 'to refute him' and to extract principles from Abu Hanifa's fatwas. Similarly, the Shafi'i Ibn Surayj wrote a refutation of Ibn Dawud's rejection of qiyas. This shows that many early usul works were polemical or defensive.
Other motivations include explaining and commenting, as with the commentaries on al-Shafi'i's Risala.
4
Recognize the trend of commentary and consolidation
The passage mentions that Shafi'i scholars wrote commentaries on al-Risala, and that some works like al-Jassas's 'Usul al-Karkhi wa al-Jassas' became famous. This indicates a move from initial polemics to more systematic expositions.
This historical development is crucial for understanding later usul texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي ولأبي بكر البردعي (1) (ت: 350هـ) كتاب (الإشراف على الأصول). هذه الفترة عكف علماء الحنفية على دراسة رسالة الشافعي للرد عليه فيما خالفهم فيه، ولاستخلاص أصول لفقههم من خلال فتاوى الإمام أبي حنيفة رحم الله في المسائل الجزئية التي عرضت له فكتب منهم عيسى بن أبان(2) ت : 220 هـ) كتابا في (خبر الواحد وكتاب (إثبات القياس)، كما صنف الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي (ت: 330 هـ ) كتاب (مآخذ الشرائع)، وكتب (ت: 340 هـ) (أصوله) المعروفة وصنف الإمام أبو بكر الجصاص (3) (ت: 370هـ) كتابه المشهور (أصول الكرخي (4) الجصاص). (3) (6) أما الشافعية فقد كتب منهم أبو العباس بن سريج (ت: 305هـ) كتاب (الرد علی ابن داود في إبطال القياس، وكتب إبراهيم بن أحمد المروزي (ت: 340هـ) كتاب (العموم والخصوص والفصول في معرفة الأصول). وألف أبو عبد الله الشيرازي (ت: 371هـ) كتاب (الفصول في الأصول)، وأنجز أبو بكر الصيمري (ت: 386هـ)، كتاب القياس والعلل . كما عكف بعضهم على شرح (الرسالة)، فشرحها أبو بكر الصيرفي (ت: 330هـ)، وأبو بكر القفال (ت: 365هـ)، كما شرحها غير هؤلاء . وقد شارك المالكية أيضًا في هذه الحركة التأليفية، فكتب أبو بكر الأبهري(6)
And for Abu Bakr al-Barda'i (d. 350 AH) is the book 'al-Ishraf 'ala al-Usul'. During this period, Hanafi scholars focused on studying al-Shafi'i's Risala to refute him in matters they differed with him, and to extract principles for their fiqh from the fatwas of Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, on the particular issues that came to him. So among them, 'Isa ibn Aban (d. 220 AH) wrote a book on 'Khabar al-Wahid' and a book 'Ithbat al-Qiyas'. Also, Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (d. 330 AH) authored 'Ma'akhidh al-Shara'i' and someone (d. 340 AH) wrote his famous 'Usul'. And Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas (d. 370 AH) authored his well-known book 'Usul al-Karkhi wa al-Jassas'. As for the Shafi'is, among them Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj (d. 305 AH) wrote a book 'al-Radd 'ala Ibn Dawud fi Ibtal al-Qiyas', and Ibrahim ibn Ahmad al-Marwazi (d. 340 AH) wrote 'al-'Umum wa al-Khusus wa al-Fusul fi Ma'rifat al-Usul'. Abu 'Abd Allah al-Shirazi (d. 371 AH) authored 'al-Fusul fi al-Usul', and Abu Bakr al-Saymari (d. 386 AH) accomplished the book 'al-Qiyas wa al-'Ilal'. Some also engaged in explaining 'al-Risala'; so Abu Bakr al-Sayrafi (d. 330 AH) explained it, and Abu Bakr al-Qaffal (d. 365 AH) explained it, as did others. The Malikis also participated in this authorship movement, so Abu Bakr al-Abhari (6) wrote.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview of early usul al-fiqh scholars and their contributions. It begins by mentioning Abu Bakr al-Barda'i and his book 'al-Ishraf 'ala al-Usul'. Then it describes the Hanafi school's engagement with al-Shafi'i's Risala, both for refutation and for deriving their own principles from Abu Hanifa's fatwas. It lists 'Isa ibn Aban's works on solitary reports and analogy, followed by al-Maturidi's work on the sources of laws. The passage mentions an anonymous author of 'Usul' from 340 AH and then highlights al-Jassas's famous 'Usul al-Karkhi wa al-Jassas'. Moving to the Shafi'is, it notes Ibn Surayj's refutation of Ibn Dawud's rejection of qiyas, al-Marwazi's book on general and specific terms and chapters on usul, al-Shirazi's 'al-Fusul fi al-Usul', and al-Saymari's work on qiyas and 'ilal. It also mentions that several scholars wrote commentaries on al-Shafi'i's Risala, including al-Sayrafi and al-Qaffal. Finally, it notes the Maliki participation through Abu Bakr al-Abhari's work. The passage serves as a survey of the prolific authorship across madhhabs during the formative period of usul al-fiqh.

Early Pioneers of Theoretical Jadal
Lists early scholars who authored theoretical works on jadal and their books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the early authors of theoretical jadal works and trace the development of jadal as a formal discipline.

Core Idea
The first seeds of theoretical jadal were sown earlier than commonly thought, with al-Ash'ari and others preceding al-Qaffal al-Shashi.

When we study jadal as a discipline, it's crucial to know who laid its foundations. This passage from a modern study on uṣūlī jadal lists the key early figures who wrote theoretical works on dialectic. It also corrects a common misconception about who was first, reminding us that the history of Islamic sciences is often more nuanced than a single starting point.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Shirazi's claim
According to Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, who was the first to author a work on jadal? Note that this claim is about the absolute first, not just among Shafi'is.
2
Spot the author's correction
The author of this passage disagrees with al-Shirazi's claim. He mentions three scholars who authored works on jadal before al-Qaffal al-Shashi. List them and their works.
These are: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (Kitab fi Adab al-Jadal), al-Ka'bi (Tajrid al-Jadal or al-Tahdhib fi al-Jadal), and Abu Ali al-Tabari (a book on jadal).
3
Match scholars to their works
For each scholar, write the title of their jadal work as given in the passage. This helps cement the association between author and text.
4
Establish a chronological timeline
Order the following scholars by their death dates: al-Ash'ari (324 AH), al-Ka'bi (329 AH), Abu Ali al-Tabari (350 AH), al-Qaffal al-Shashi (365 AH), al-Darki (375 AH). This shows the progression of theoretical jadal authorship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الخامس : التأليف النظري في الجدل الأصولي خلال هذه المرحلة
إذا كانت هذه المرحلة، وهي التي سميناها بمرحلة النشأة والتأسيس. شهدت تركيز المؤلفات في الجدل الأصولي على ما كان منها في صورته التطبيقية، فإنها مع ذلك قد شهدت ظهور البذور الأولى للتأليف في الجدل الأصولي في صورته النظرية . وقد ذهب الإمام أبو إسحاق الشيرازي إلى أن أول من ألف في الجدل هو الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن علي بن إسماعيل، الفقيه الشافعي المعروف بالقفال الكبير (ت: 365 هـ). لكن الذي يبدو من استقراء إنتاج الأصوليين في هذا الميدان أن هناك من سبق الشاشي إلى هذا، وإن كان هو أول الشافعية سبقا إلى التأليف في الجدل. فقد سبقه مثلا الإمام أبو الحسن الأشعري (ت : 324هـ)، الذي صنف كتابا في أدب الجدل. كما سبقه أيضًا الإمام الكعبي (ت: 329هـ)، الذي ألف كتاب (تجريد الجدل) أو التهذيب في الجدل. وكذلك الإمام أبو علي الطبري (ت: 350هـ)، الذي ذكر علماء التراجم من بين مؤلفاته كتاب في الجدل. وقد جاء بعد القفال الشاشي عدد من العلماء، ساهموا هم أيضًا في بناء نظرية الجدل، ومن هؤلاء الإمام أبو القاسم الداركي (ت: 375 هـ) مؤلف كتاب (المدخل في الجدل).
The fifth demand: Theoretical authorship in fundamentalist dialectic during this stage. If this stage, which we called the stage of emergence and foundation, witnessed the concentration of works in fundamentalist dialectic on what was in its applied form, yet it nevertheless witnessed the appearance of the first seeds of authorship in fundamentalist dialectic in its theoretical form. Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi held that the first to author in dialectic was Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad bin Ali bin Ismail, the Shafi'i jurist known as al-Qaffal al-Kabir (d. 365 AH). But what appears from surveying the production of fundamentalists in this field is that there were those who preceded al-Shashi in this, although he was the first of the Shafi'is to take the lead in authorship in dialectic. For example, Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (d. 324 AH) preceded him, who composed a book on the etiquette of dialectic. Also preceded him Imam al-Ka'bi (d. 329 AH), who authored the book 'Tajrid al-Jadal' or 'al-Tahdhib fi al-Jadal'. Likewise, Imam Abu Ali al-Tabari (d. 350 AH), whom the biographical scholars mentioned among his works a book on dialectic. And after al-Qaffal al-Shashi came a number of scholars who also contributed to building the theory of dialectic, among them Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Darki (d. 375 AH), author of the book 'al-Madkhal fi al-Jadal'.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a historical survey of early theoretical works on jadal (dialectic) within the Islamic legal tradition. The author is discussing the fifth section of his book, which focuses on the emergence of theoretical writings on jadal. He notes that while earlier works were largely applied (practical), this period saw the beginnings of theoretical treatments. The central claim is that Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi considered al-Qaffal al-Shashi to be the first author in jadal. However, the author qualifies this by stating that a survey of earlier productions shows that others preceded al-Shashi, though he was the first among the Shafi'is. The author then lists several predecessors: Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who wrote a work on the etiquette of jadal; Imam al-Ka'bi, who authored 'Tajrid al-Jadal' or 'al-Tahdhib fi al-Jadal'; and Imam Abu Ali al-Tabari, whose works include a book on jadal. Following al-Qaffal al-Shashi, other scholars contributed, such as Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Darki with his 'al-Madkhal fi al-Jadal'. This passage is purely biographical and historical, establishing a timeline of key figures who shaped the theoretical framework of jadal.

Early Contributors to Jadal Theory
Author lists early scholars who contributed to jadal theory before al-Baqillani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the early scholars of jadal before al-Baqillani and their key works.

Core Idea
Jadal theory has a history; these three scholars laid its groundwork before al-Baqillani.

The development of jadal (dialectical disputation) in usul al-fiqh did not begin with al-Baqillani. This passage introduces three earlier scholars who authored foundational works on jadal. Understanding their contributions helps situate the later systematization of jadal and highlights the continuity of this intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scholar
Find Imam al-Ka'bi (d. 329 AH) in the passage. Note his work on jadal, either titled 'Tajrid al-Jadal' or 'al-Tahdhib fi al-Jadal'.
Al-Ka'bi was a Mu'tazili scholar.
2
Identify the second scholar
Find Imam Abu Ali al-Tabari (d. 350 AH). The passage mentions that biographers list a book on jadal among his works, but the title is not given.
Al-Tabari was a Shafi'i jurist.
3
Identify the third scholar
Find Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Darki (d. 375 AH). He authored 'al-Madkhal fi al-Jadal' (Introduction to Jadal).
Al-Darki came after al-Qaffal al-Shashi.
4
Establish timeline and context
Order the scholars by death date: al-Ka'bi (329), al-Tabari (350), al-Darki (375). These dates place them before al-Baqillani (d. 403 AH), showing a pre-existing tradition of jadal literature.

Source Text

كما سبقه أيضًا الإمام الكعبي (ت: 329هـ)، الذي ألف كتاب (تجريد الجدل) أو التهذيب في الجدل. وكذلك الإمام أبو علي الطبري (ت: 350هـ)، الذي ذكر علماء التراجم من بين مؤلفاته كتاب في الجدل. وقد جاء بعد القفال الشاشي عدد من العلماء، ساهموا هم أيضًا في بناء نظرية الجدل، ومن هؤلاء الإمام أبو القاسم الداركي (ت: 375 هـ) مؤلف كتاب (المدخل في الجدل).
Also preceded by Imam al-Ka'bi (d. 329 AH), who authored the book 'Tajrid al-Jadal' or 'al-Tahdhib fi al-Jadal'. Commentary
This passage lists early contributors to the theory of jadal (dialectical disputation) in usul al-fiqh, before the later developmental phase. It mentions three key figures: first, Imam al-Ka'bi (d. 329 AH), a Mu'tazili scholar who wrote a work titled either 'Tajrid al-Jadal' or 'al-Tahdhib fi al-Jadal' (the precise title is uncertain). Second, Imam Abu Ali al-Tabari (d. 350 AH), a Shafi'i jurist, whose biographical entries note a book on jadal among his works. Third, after al-Qaffal al-Shashi (a noted Shafi'i jurist of the previous generation), there were other scholars, including Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Darki (d. 375 AH), who authored 'al-Madkhal fi al-Jadal' (Introduction to Jadal). The passage thus establishes a lineage of early writings on jadal, setting the stage for the more systematic development that follows.

The Developmental Phase of Jadal in Usul al-Fiqh
Author defines the developmental phase of jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the temporal boundaries and two phases (applied and theoretical) in the development of jadal as described by the author.

Core Idea
Jadal evolved from practical debates into a formal theory of disputation.

This passage marks a crucial turning point in the history of usul al-fiqh jadal. The author defines a period of development that begins with al-Baqillani and ends with al-Razi, noting a shift from applied debate to theoretical rule-building.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timeline
Find the start and end dates mentioned: the 4th century AH to the end of the 6th century AH (al-Baqillani d. 403 AH, al-Razi d. 606 AH).
This shows the long duration of this developmental stage.
2
Note the key figures
The passage names al-Baqillani, 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Mu'tazili, and al-Razi as pivotal scholars.
They represent both the applied and theoretical sides.
3
Distinguish the two phases
The author states that jadal began as applied (practical debates) and later theoretical studies emerged to extract rules and principles.
This sequence is crucial for understanding jadal's disciplinary growth.

يمكن اعتبار أن مرحلة التطور والتكامل في البحث الجدلي في أصول الفقه، تبدأ مع الإمام أبي بكر الباقلاني الذي أعطى دفعا قويا للبحث الجدلي الأصولي رفقة الإمام عبد الجبار المعتزلي، وذلك منذ بداية القرن الرابع الهجري. وتنتهي هذه المرحلة مباشرة بنهاية القرن السادس الهجري، أي بعد الإمام الرازي الذي توفي في أوائل القرن السابع الهجري (606 هـ). في هذه المرحلة شهد البحث الجدلي في أصول الفقه تطورًا متصاعدًا، ابتدأ تطبيقيا أول الأمر، ثم سرعان ما ظهرت إلى جانب ذلك الدراسات النظرية التي عملت على استخلاص نظرية الجدل وبناء قواعدها ومبادئها، لذلك سنتتبع في هذا المبحث التطور المتصاعد للجدل الأصولي من خلال مبحثين، نخصص أولهما للجدل التطبيقي والثاني للدراسات النظرية في الجدل عند الأصوليين. المطلب الأول : تطور الجدل الأصولي في صورته التطبيقية. يبتدئ هذا التطور كما سبق أن قلت الإمام أبي بكر الباقلاني الذي عاش خلال القرن الرابع الهجري، إذ ولد حوالي سنة 338هـ، وتوفي سنة 403 هـ، وقد اشتهر في حياته بطول نفسه في المناظرات وقدرته على محاججة الخصوم ومجادلتهم والظهور عليهم ؛ وقد ذكر ابن خلكان أن الباقلاني كان طويل النفس في المناظرة، مشهورًا بذلك، فجرى يوما بينه وبين أبي سعيد الهاروني مناظرة
It can be considered that the stage of development and integration in jadal research in usul al-fiqh begins with Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, who gave a strong impetus to uṣūlī jadal research alongside Imam 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Mu'tazili, starting from the beginning of the fourth century AH. And this stage ends directly at the end of the sixth century AH, that is, after Imam al-Razi who died at the beginning of the seventh century AH (606 AH). In this stage, jadal research in usul al-fiqh witnessed an ascending development, starting practically at first, then soon alongside that appeared theoretical studies that worked on extracting the theory of jadal and building its rules and principles. Therefore, we will follow in this section the ascending development of uṣūlī jadal through two sections: we devote the first to applied jadal and the second to theoretical studies in jadal among the Uṣūliyyīn. The first sub-section: The development of uṣūlī jadal in its applied form. This development begins, as I said earlier, with Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani who lived during the fourth century AH, as he was born around 338 AH and died in 403 AH. During his life, he was famous for his long breath in debates and his ability to argue with opponents and dispute with them and overcome them. And Ibn Khallikan mentioned that al-Baqillani had a long breath in debate, being famous for that, so one day a debate took place between him and Abu Sa'id al-Haruni.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage introduces the second main section of the book, which covers the stage of development and integration in jadal within usul al-fiqh. The author defines the temporal boundaries: this stage begins with Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (d. 403 AH) and Imam 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Mu'tazili (d. 415 AH) at the start of the 4th century AH, and ends at the close of the 6th century AH, after Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606 AH). The author notes that jadal research evolved from practical application to theoretical study, with scholars extracting rules and principles. The author then announces a plan to examine this development in two parts: applied jadal and theoretical studies. The first sub-section focuses on applied jadal, beginning with al-Baqillani. The author provides biographical details: al-Baqillani was born around 338 AH and died in 403 AH. He was renowned for his stamina in debates and his ability to overcome opponents. The passage references Ibn Khallikan's report of a debate between al-Baqillani and Abu Sa'id al-Haruni, illustrating his prowess.

Al-Baqillani's Role in Developing Jadal in Usul al-Fiqh
Author describes al-Baqillani's role in the second stage of jadal development.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe al-Baqillani's contributions to jadal and explain how his work advanced dialectical method in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani transformed jadal from a practical skill into a systematic tool for refuting opponents in usul al-fiqh.

The second stage of jadal development in usul al-fiqh begins with Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, an Ash'ari theologian who brought his dialectical prowess to the field. His book 'al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad' became the cornerstone for later usul scholars, and his method of debate—characterized by lengthy, overwhelming arguments—set a new standard. This lesson examines his role and the historical context of this transformative period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Historical Period
Locate when al-Baqillani lived (born 338 AH, died 403 AH) and note that this stage ends with al-Razi (d. 606 AH). Recognize that jadal evolved from practical to theoretical during this time.
This timeline helps contextualize al-Baqillani's influence.
2
Analyze the Anecdote of Debate
Read the anecdote where al-Baqillani challenged his opponent to repeat his words or forgo an answer. Consider how this illustrates his 'long breath' and dominance in debate.
Such anecdotes reveal the practical jadal style of the era.
3
Connect Theology to Methodology
Al-Baqillani was an Ash'ari theologian. Note how his theological background influenced his approach to usul al-fiqh, particularly in refuting Mu'tazili principles.
This shows the interplay between kalam and usul.
4
Assess the Significance of 'al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad'
The passage calls this book the first comprehensive work on usul al-fiqh. Identify its dialectical aim: to invalidate Mu'tazili rules like rational good/evil and the obligation of the optimal on God.
This established a model for later usul works.
5
Recognize the Shift to Theoretical Jadal
The author mentions that jadal moved from applied to theoretical studies during this stage. Al-Baqillani's book contributed to extracting principles of jadal.
This shift laid the groundwork for later systematic works on jadal.
